Eggeling
  1. He takes the spade, with (V─Бj. S. VI, 1), ‘I take thee, at the impulse of the divine Savitr╠е, with the arms of the A┼Ыvins, with the hands of P┼лshan: thou art a woman.’ The significance of that formula is the same (as before); and that spade (abhri, fem.) is indeed female: therefore he says ’thou art a woman.’

Eggeling
  1. He then digs, and throws up a heap of earth towards the east. He digs the hole, making it equal (in depth) with the (unhewn) bottom part (of the stake). In front of it he lays down the stake with the top towards the east. Thereon he puts sacrificial grass of the same size, and thereupon he puts the chip of the stake. In front on the (north) side (of the stake) he puts down the head-piece 3. The sprinkling-water has barley-corns mixed with it: the significance of this is the same (as before 4).

Eggeling
  1. He throws the barley-corns in with, ‘Thou art barley (yava), keep thou (yavaya) from us the haters, keep from us the enemies!’ There is nothing obscure in this. He then sprinkles: the significance of the sprinkling is one and the same: he thereby renders it sacrificially pure.

Eggeling
  1. Eggeling
  1. He then throws in the (first) chip 9 of the stake. Now that chip of the outer (bark) doubtless is the vigour of trees; hence, when a chip of their outer (bark) is cut off they dry up, for it is their vigour. Hence, when he throws in the chip of the stake, he does so thinking, ‘I will plant it (the stake) full of vigour.’ The reason why it is this (chip) and no other, is that this one has been produced with a formula, is sacrificially pure: therefore he throws in the chip of the stake.

Eggeling
  1. He throws it in with (V─Бj. S. VI, 2), ‘Thou art a leader, easy of access to the Unnetr╠еs 10;’ for that (chip) is cut from it in front, wherefore he says, ‘Thou art a leader, easy of access to the Unnetr╠еs.’ ‘Be thou mindful of this: it will stand upon thee!’ for it (the stake) will indeed stand on it, wherefore he says, ‘Be thou mindful of this: it will stand upon thee.’

Eggeling
  1. Having then taken out ghee with the dipping-spoon, he offers it into the hole, ’lest the evil spirits should rise from below:’ ghee is a thunderbolt, he

thus repels the evil spirits by means of the thunderbolt, and thus the evil spirits do not rise from below. Having then gone round to the front, he sits down facing the north and anoints the stake. He says (to the Hotr╠е), ‘Recite to the stake as it is anointed 11!’

Eggeling
  1. He anoints it with, ‘The divine Savitr╠е anoint thee with sweet drink (milk)!’ for Savitr╠е is the impeller (prasavitr╠е) of the gods, and that stake is in reality the sacrificer himself; and sweet drink is everything here; he thus puts it in connection with all that, and Savitr╠е, the impeller, impels it for him: therefore he says, ‘The divine Savitr╠е anoint thee with sweet drink!’

Eggeling
  1. Having then anointed the top-ring on both sides, he puts it on (the stake) with, ‘To the full-berried plants–thee!’ for that (top-ring) is as its berry. And as to its being, as it were, contracted in the middle, the berry 14 here on trees is fastened (to the stalk) sideways; what connecting part there is between (the fruit and stalk) pressed in, as it were, that he thereby makes it. This is why it is, as it were, contracted in the middle.

Eggeling
  1. He anoints from top to bottom the (corner) facing the fire; for the (corner) facing the fire is the sacrificer, and the ghee is sap: with sap he thus anoints the sacrificer; therefore he anoints from top to bottom the (corner) facing the fire. He then

grasps the girding-part all round, and says (to the Hotr╠е), ‘Recite to the (stake) being set up!’

Eggeling
  1. He raises it with, ‘With thy crest thou hast touched the sky; with thy middle thou hast filled the air; with thy foot thou hast steadied the earth;’–the sacrificial stake being a thunderbolt, (he raises it) for the conquering of these worlds; with that thunderbolt he gains these worlds, and deprives his enemies of their share in these worlds.

рдЕрде рдорд┐рдиреЛрддрд┐- “рдпрд╛ рддреЗ рдзрд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпреБрд╢реНрдорд╕рд┐ рдЧрдордзреНрдпреИ рдпрддреНрд░ рдЧрд╛рд╡реЛ рднреВрд░рд┐рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд╛ рд╜рдЕрдпрд╛рд╕рдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░рд╛рд╣ рддрджреБрд░реБрдЧрд╛рдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреЛрдГ рдкрд░рдордВ рдкрджрдорд╡рднрд╛рд░рд┐ рднреВрд░рд┐”- (рд╡рд╛. рд╕рдВ. рем ред рей) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдПрддрдпрд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрд╛ рдорд┐рдиреЛрддрд┐ ред рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН ред рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЛ рдпреВрдкрдГ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрд╛ рдорд┐рдиреЛрддрд┐ рее резрел рее

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

Eggeling
  1. He then plants it (in the hole) with (V─Бj. S. VI, 3), ‘To what resorts of thine we long to go where are the swift-footed, many-horned kine; there, forsooth, was imprinted wide-striding Vishс╣Зu’s highest mighty foot-step.’ With this trishс╣нubh verse he plants it; the trishс╣нubh is a thunderbolt, as the sacrificial stake is a thunderbolt; therefore he plants it with a trishс╣нubh verse.

рдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдорд╛рд╣- рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдореН’ ‘рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН’ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреНрдпрднрд┐рдореБрдЦрдВ ‘рдорд┐рдиреЛрддрд┐’ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рд╡рд┐рдкрдХреНрд╖реЗ рджреЛрд╖рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЗрди рджреНрд░рдврдпрддрд┐- рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдиреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░рд┐рддрд┐ ред ‘рд╕рдГ’ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реНрдпреБрдГ ‘рдпрджреН’ рдпрджрд┐ ‘рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ’ рд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рддреН ‘рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдореНтАЩ тАШрд╣реНрд╡рд▓рдпреЗрддреН’ рдЪрд╛рд▓рдпреЗрддреН ‘рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреН’ ‘рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ’ рдЕрдкрд┐ ‘рд╣реНрд╡рд▓реЗрддреН’ рдкрд╢реНрдпреЗрддреН, ‘рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН’ ‘рд╕рдореНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧреНрдирд┐рдВ’ рдорд┐рдиреБрдпрд╛рддреН рее рдЕрде рдкрд░реНрдпреВрд╣рддреАрддрд┐ 18 ред рдореГрджрд╛рдореЗрдХреАрднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкрд╛рджрдиреЗ рдкрд░реНрдпрд╣рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдореМрджреБрдореНрдмрд░реНрдпрд╛рдореБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН (рд╢. рдк. рдмреНрд░рд╛. рей ред рем ред рез ред резрен-резреп) рдЕрддреНрд░ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗ рдЙрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рее резрем рее

Eggeling
  1. That (corner which was) facing the fire he places opposite the fire; for the (corner) facing the fire is the sacrificer, and the sacrifice is fire. Hence were he to turn the fire-corner aside from the fire, the sacrificer would assuredly turn aside from the sacrifice; therefore he places the (corner which was) facing the fire opposite the fire. He then heaps up (earth) round it and presses it firmly all round, and pours water thereon 19.

рдордиреНрддреНрд░рддрд╛рддреНрдкрд░реНрдпрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╖реНрдЯреЗ- рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдВ рд╡рд╛ рдПрд╖ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ ред ‘рдЙрджрд╢рд┐рд╢реНрд░рд┐рдпрддреН’- рдЗрддрд┐, тАЬрд╢реНрд░рд┐рдЮреН рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛рдпрд╛рдореН"- (рдзрд╛. рдкрд╛. репреиреи) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд▓реБрдЩрд┐ рд░реВрдкрдореН ред ‘рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддрд┐рдореН’ рд╡рд┐рдЬрдпрдореН ред рдХрд░реНрдордгрд╛рдВ рдмрд╣реБрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд┐рддреЗрд░реЗрдХрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреЗрдХрд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрджреНрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореН ред рдЪрддреБрд░реНрдердкрд╛рджреЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдгрдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣- рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░реЛ рд╡реИ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕реНрдп рджреЗрд╡рддреЗрддрд┐ рее репрен рее

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he makes (the sacrificer) say while touching it (V─Бj. S. VI, 4; Rig-veda I, 22, 19), ‘See ye the deeds of Vishс╣Зu, whereby he beheld the sacred ordinances, Indra’s allied

friend!’ For he who has set up the sacrificial stake has hurled the thunderbolt: ‘See ye Vishс╣Зu’s conquest!’ he means to say when he says, ‘See ye the deeds of Vishс╣Зu, whereby he beheld the sacred ordinances, Indra’s allied friend.’ Indra, forsooth, is the deity of the sacrifice, and the sacrificial stake belongs to Vishс╣Зu; he thereby connects it with Indra; therefore he says, ‘Indra’s allied friend.’

Eggeling
  1. He then looks up at the top-ring with (V─Бj. S. VI, 5; Rig-veda I, 22, 20), ‘The wise ever behold that highest step of Vishс╣Зu, fixed like an eye in the heaven.’ For he who has set up the sacrificial stake has hurled the thunderbolt: ‘See ye that conquest of Vishс╣Зu!’ he means to say when he says, ‘The wise ever behold that highest step of Vishс╣Зu, fixed like an eye in the heaven.’

Eggeling
  1. He then girds (the stake with a rope of ku┼Ыa-grass). Now it is to cover its nakedness that he girds it; wherefore he girds it in this place (viz. on a level with the sacrificer’s navel), for it is thus that this (nether) garment is (slung round) 21. He thereby puts food into him, for it is there that the food settles; therefore he girds it at that place.

Eggeling
  1. He girds it with a triple (rope), for threefold is food, and food means cattle; and (there is) the father and the mother, and what is born is the third; therefore he girds it with a triple (rope).

Eggeling
  1. Thereupon he inserts a chip of the stake (under the rope) with, ‘Thou art the son of the sky.’ For it is doubtless the offspring of that (sacrificial stake); hence if there be the full number of eleven stakes 23, let him insert in each its own (chip) without confounding them; and his offspring is born orderly and not foolish. But whosoever inserts them in confusion, not its own in each, verily his offspring is born disorderly and foolish; therefore let him insert its own in each without confounding them.

Eggeling
  1. Moreover, that chip of the stake is made an ascent to the heavenly world; there is this girdle-rope; after the rope the chip of the stake; after the chip of the stake the top-ring; and from the top-ring one reaches the heavenly world.

Eggeling
  1. And as to why it is called svaru (‘very sore’),–that (chip) is cut off from that (stake), and thus is its own (sva) sore (arus); therefore it is called ‘svaru.’

Eggeling
  1. With that part of it which is dug in, he gains the world of the Fathers; and with what is above the dug-in part, up to the girdle-rope, he gains the world of men; and with what is above the rope, up to the top-ring, he gains the world of the gods; and what (space of) two or three fingersтАЩ breadths

there is above the top-ring,–the gods called the ‘Blessed 24,’–their world he therewith gains; verily, whosoever thus knows this, he becomes one of the same world with the blessed gods.

Eggeling
  1. That (sacrificial stake) he sets up on the fore-part (of the altar); for the stake is a thunderbolt, as the club is a thunderbolt. But in hurling the club one takes hold of its fore-part; and that (stake) is the fore-part of the sacrifice; therefore he sets it up on the fore-part (of the altar).

Eggeling
  1. Verily, by means of the sacrifice the gods gained that supreme authority which they now wield. They spake, ‘How may this (world) of ours be made unattainable to men?’ They sipped the sap of the sacrifice, as bees would suck out honey, and having drained the sacrifice and scattered it by means of the sacrificial stake, they disappeared. And because they scattered (yopaya) therewith, therefore it is called y┼лpa (sacrificial stake). At the head stands intelligence, at the head swiftness of thought; therefore he sets it up on the fore-part (of the altar).

рд╕рд╛рдпрдгрдГ

рд╕ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╢реНрд░рд┐рд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ ред рд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯрдореН рее реирео рее

Eggeling
  1. It is eight-cornered; for the g─Бyatr─л metre consists of eight syllables, and the g─Бyatr─л is the fore-part of the sacrifice, as this (stake) is the forepart of the sacrifice; therefore it is eight-cornered.

S. VI, 21), ‘May thy smoke rise up to the sky, thy light to the heavens! fill the earth with ashes, Hail!’
